Let me use a DIFFERENT approach.\n    \n    # I'll use the idea of \"boomerang attack\" or \"slide attack\".\n    # Or just encrypt a plaintext and try to find key[5] that\n    # makes the decrypted last round \"look right\".\n    \n    # Actually, I think the easiest is:\n    # Since there are only 65536 possible key[5] values,\n    # I can just encrypt ONE plaintext and for each candidate key[5],\n    # compute L3 = getleft(C) ^ f(R3 ^ key[5]).\n    # If the MSB of L3 matches the MSB of something predictable, \n    # we can narrow down.\n    \n    # But how to verify? Let me use TWO plaintexts with different left halves.\n    \n    # Idea: For two plaintexts P1 and P2 with left halves L1 and L2,\n    # both with same right half.\n    # After whitening: L0_1 = L1 ^ k0, L0_2 = L2 ^ k0 (diff = L1 ^ L2 = ΔL)\n    # After pre-round: R0_1 = (R ^ k1) ^ L0_1, R0_2 = (R ^ k1) ^ L0_2\n    # Diff in R0 = ΔL\n    # \n    # Round 0: F input diff = ΔL, so F output diff = ΔF (depends on ΔL)\n    # R1_1 = L0_1 ^ F(...), R1_2 = L0_2 ^ F(...)\n    # R1 diff = ΔL ^ ΔF\n    # L1 diff = ΔL\n    # \n    # Round 1: F input diff = ΔL ^ ΔF... this gets messy.\n    \n    # Let me try a completely different approach.\n    # What if I use the fact that the F-function is weak and can be inverted\n    # byte by byte for a given input?\n    \n    # For a given candidate key[5], I can compute:\n    # R3 = getright(C) ^ getleft(C)\n    # L3 = getleft(C) ^ f(R3 ^ key[5])\n    # \n    # Now, from round 2:\n    # R3 = L2 ^ f(R2 ^ key[4])\n    # L3 = R2\n    # \n    # So: R3 = L2 ^ f(L3 ^ key[4])\n    # Thus: L2 = R3 ^ f(L3 ^ key[4])\n    # \n    # And L2 = R1 (from round 1 swap).\n    # So: R1 = R3 ^ f(L3 ^ key[4])\n    # \n    # Now, R1 is also equal to: R1 = L0 ^ f(R0 ^ key[2])\n    # \n    # So: L0 ^ f(R0 ^ key[2]) = R3 ^ f(L3 ^ key[4])\n    # Thus: f(R0 ^ key[2]) = L0 ^ R3 ^ f(L3 ^ key[4])\n    # \n    # R0 = (right ^ key[1]) ^ L0\n    # \n    # This is one equation with unknowns key[0], key[1], key[2], key[4].\n    # \n    # If I take another plaintext P' with different left and same right:\n    # L0' = left' ^ key[0]\n    # R0' = (right' ^ key[1]) ^ L0' = (same right ^ key[1]) ^ L0'\n    # \n    # f(R0' ^ key[2]) = L0' ^ R3' ^ f(L3' ^ key[4])\n    # \n    # Subtracting (XOR):\n    # f(R0 ^ key[2]) ^ f(R0' ^ key[2]) = (L0 ^ L0') ^ (R3 ^ R3') ^ (f(L3 ^ key[4]) ^ f(L3' ^ key[4]))\n    # \n    # The left side depends on key[2]. The right side depends on key[4] and known values.\n    # \n    # This is STILL complex.\n    \n    # Let me just try to brute-force all 65536 key[5] values using a \n    # simple statistical test.\n    \n    print(\"Starting attack...\", file=sys.stderr)\n    \n    # We'll encrypt 4 plaintexts\n    plaintexts = []\n    ciphertexts = []\n    \n    # Choose plaintexts with varying left halves\n    import random\n    random.seed(12345)\n    for i in range(4):\n        left = random.randint(0, 0xFFFFFFFF)\n        right = random.randint(0, 0xFFFFFFFF)\n        pt = merge(left, right)\n        ct = encrypt_fn(pt)\n        plaintexts.append(pt)\n        ciphertexts.append(ct)\n        print(f\"  P{i}: left={hex(left)}, right={hex(right)}\", file=sys.stderr)\n        print(f\"  C{i}: {hex(ct)}\", file=sys.stderr)\n    \n    # Precompute all possible seeds -> keys\n    # Actually, key[5] = (seed * 1234567) & 0xFFFFFFFF\n    # So we can map from seed to key[5] easily\n    \n    # For each candidate key[5], compute R3 and L3 for all plaintexts\n    # and check if the relationship holds\n    \n    # The relationship we'll use:\n    # R3 = R1 ^ f(L3 ^ key[4])\n    # L3 = R0 ^ f(R1 ^ key[3])\n    # \n    # For two pairs (P1, C1) and (P2, C2), with the correct key[5],\n    # we get (L3_1, R3_1) and (L3_2, R3_2).\n    # Then:\n    # R1_1 = R3_1 ^ f(L3_1 ^ key[4])\n    # R1_2 = R3_2 ^ f(L3_2 ^ key[4])\n    # \n    # And also:\n    # L3_1 = R0_1 ^ f(R1_1 ^ key[3])\n    # L3_2 = R0_2 ^ f(R1_2 ^ key[3])\n    # \n    # => R0_1 = L3_1 ^ f(R1_1 ^ key[3])\n    # => R0_2 = L3_2 ^ f(R1_2 ^ key[3])\n    # \n    # But R0 = (right ^ key[1]) ^ L0 = (right ^ key[1]) ^ (left ^ key[0])\n    # \n    # So R0_1 ^ R0_2 = (left_1 ^ left_2) ^ (right_1 ^ right_2) ... wait:\n    # R0 = (right ^ key[1]) ^ (left ^ key[0]) = right ^ left ^ key[0] ^ key[1]\n    # Actually: L0 = left ^ key[0]\n    # R0 = (right ^ key[1]) ^ L0 = right ^ key[1] ^ left ^ key[0] = left ^ right ^ key[0] ^ key[1]\n    # \n    # So R0 depends on plaintext in a known way (left ^ right) plus unknown constants (key[0] ^ key[1]).\n    # \n    # Thus: R0_1 ^ R0_2 = (left_1 ^ right_1) ^ (left_2 ^ right_2)  [since key[0] ^ key[1] cancels]\n    # \n    # Similarly, L0 = left ^ key[0], so L0_1 ^ L0_2 = left_1 ^ left_2.\n    # \n    # And R1 = L0 ^ f(R0 ^ key[2])\n    # So R1_1 ^ R1_2 = (left_1 ^ left_2) ^ (f(R0_1 ^ key[2]) ^ f(R0_2 ^ key[2]))\n    # \n    # This is getting closer but still has unknown key[2].\n    \n    # Let me try a completely different approach: \n    # Just use 6 chosen plaintexts and brute-force both key[4] and key[5] simultaneously?\n    # That's 65536^2 = 4.3 billion, too many.\n    \n    # WAIT! I can use a meet-in-the-middle approach!\n    \n    # For each candidate key[5]:\n    #   Compute L3_i, R3_i for each plaintext i\n    # For each candidate key[4]:\n    #   Compute expected R3_i (call it R3_expected_i) = L2_i ^ f(R2_i ^ key[4]) ... but we don't know L2_i and R2_i\n    \n    # Actually, let me think about this differently.\n    \n    # I'll use the DIFFERENTIAL approach.\n    # \n    # Choose pairs (P, P') where P' = P ^ 0x8080000000000000 (left half diff = 0x80800000)\n    # As we saw, after round 0, the difference propagates.\n    # The ciphertext difference gives information about key[5].\n    \n    # Let me implement this properly.\n    \n    print(\"\\nTrying differential approach...\", file=sys.stderr)\n    \n    # Use a specific differential: \n    # Set L = 0x00000000, R = 0x00000000\n    # P0 = merge(L, R) = 0x0000000000000000\n    # P1 = merge(L ^ 0x80800000, R) = 0x8080000000000000\n    \n    P0 = 0x0000000000000000\n    P1 = 0x8080000000000000\n    \n    C0 = encrypt_fn(P0)\n    C1 = encrypt_fn(P1)\n    \n    print(f\"P0: {hex(P0)}, C0: {hex(C0)}\", file=sys.stderr)\n    print(f\"P1: {hex(P1)}, C1: {hex(C1)}\", file=sys.stderr)\n    \n    # Let's compute the ciphertext difference\n    diff_C = C0 ^ C1\n    print(f\"C0 ^ C1: {hex(diff_C)}\", file=sys.stderr)\n    \n    # Now, we can try to brute-force key[5] by checking if the decrypted values\n    # satisfy some property.\n    \n    # Actually, let me try the simplest thing: \n    # brute-force all 65536 key[5] values and check consistency across multiple pairs.\n    \n    # Let me use 3 plaintexts with known relationships and a consistency check.\n    \n    print(\"\\nBrute-forcing key[5] from seed space...\", file=sys.stderr)\n    \n    # Encrypt 3 plaintexts\n    P = [0x0000000000000000, 0x1111111111111111, 0x2222222222222222]\n    C = [encrypt_fn(p) for p in P]\n    \n    # Try all possible seeds for key[5]\n    for seed5 in range(65536):\n        k5 = (seed5 * 1234567) & 0xFFFFFFFF\n        \n        # Compute R3 and L3 for each ciphertext\n        valid = True\n        L3_vals = []\n        R3_vals = []\n        for ct in C:\n            R3 = getright(ct) ^ getleft(ct)\n            L3 = getleft(ct) ^ f_function(R3 ^ k5)\n            L3_vals.append(L3)\n            R3_vals.append(R3)\n        \n        # The relationship between pairs:\n        # For each pair (i, j), we have:\n        # R3_i = R1_i ^ f(L3_i ^ key[4])\n        # R3_j = R1_j ^ f(L3_j ^ key[4])\n        # \n        # Also R1_i = L0_i ^ f(R0_i ^ key[2])\n        # And R1_j = L0_j ^ f(R0_j ^ key[2])\n        # \n        # L0_i = left_i ^ key[0]\n        # R0_i = (right_i ^ key[1]) ^ L0_i = left_i ^ right_i ^ key[0] ^ key[1]\n        # \n        # So L0_i ^ L0_j = left_i ^ left_j  (key[0] cancels)\n        # R0_i ^ R0_j = (left_i ^ right_i) ^ (left_j ^ right_j)  (key[0] ^ key[1] cancels)\n        # \n        # This is getting too complex without more structure.\n        pass\n    \n    print(\"This approach isn't working, trying different method...\", file=sys.stderr)\n    \n    # Let me try the actual differential attack.\n    # Since the F-function has the property that for input diff 0x80800000,\n    # the output diff is always 0x02000000, I can trace differences through rounds.\n    \n    # Let me choose pairs that make the difference after round 2 controllable.\n    \n    return 0  # Placeholder\n\nif __name__ == \"__main__\":\n    # Test with known keys\n    import feal\n    feal.create_random_keys()\n    print(f\"Actual key[5]: {hex(feal.key[5])}\", file=sys.stderr)\n    result = attack(feal.encrypt)\n    print(f\"Recovered: {hex(result)}\", file=sys.stderr)\nENDSCRIPT\npython3 /app/attack.py\n",
      "duration": 1.0
    }
  ],
  "task_complete": false
}
```
